123113 LVINLBVWd
123131 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
123446 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
123846 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
124030 GPIB status vector:
124051 status[0] - Device Clear State
124082  status[1] - Device Trigger State
124116  status[2] - Listener Active State
124152 status[3] - Talker Active State
124185 status[4] - Attention line asserted
124222 status[5] -
124234 Controller In Charge
124255  status[6] - Remote State
124281  status[7] - Lockout State
124309 status[8] - I/O Completed 
124337 status[9] - not used
124358  status[10]- not used
124380  status[11]- not used
124403 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
124443 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
124475  status[14]- Timeout occured
124504  status[15]- GPIB error detected
124540 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
124593 GPIB Error:
124610 -No error
124625 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
124664 -No listeners detected on write
124701 -Controller not addressed correctly
124742 -Invalid argument(s)
124769 (perhaps bad address string????)
124807 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
124845 -I/O operation aborted
124873 -hardware not present
124900 -DMA error
124916 -DMA bus timeout
124938 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
124977 progress
124991 -function not implemented
125022 -file system error
125046 -shareable board exclusively owned
125086 -GPIB bus error (commands)
125118 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
125146 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
125179 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
125269 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
125603 GPIB status vector:
125624 status[0] - Device Clear State
125655  status[1] - Device Trigger State
125689  status[2] - Listener Active State
125725 status[3] - Talker Active State
125758 status[4] - Attention line asserted
125795 status[5] -
125807 Controller In Charge
125828  status[6] - Remote State
125854  status[7] - Lockout State
125882 status[8] - I/O Completed 
125910 status[9] - not used
125931  status[10]- not used
125953  status[11]- not used
125976 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
126016 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
126048  status[14]- Timeout occured
126077  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

182469 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set. 
182523 GPIB Error:
182540 -No error
182555 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
182594 -No listeners detected on write
182631 -Controller not addressed correctly
182672 -Invalid argument(s)
182699 (perhaps bad address string????)
182737 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
182775 -I/O operation aborted
182803 -hardware not present
182830 -DMA error
182846 -DMA bus timeout
182868 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
182907 progress
182921 -function not implemented
182952 -file system error
182976 -shareable board exclusively owned
183016 -GPIB bus error (commands)
183048 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
183076 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
183109 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
183201 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
183385 GPIB status vector:
183406 status[0] - Device Clear State
183437  status[1] - Device Trigger State
183471  status[2] - Listener Active State
183507 status[3] - Talker Active State
183540 status[4] - Attention line asserted
183577 status[5] -
183589 Controller In Charge
183610  status[6] - Remote State
183636  status[7] - Lockout State
183664 status[8] - I/O Completed 
183692 status[9] - not used
183713  status[10]- not used
183735  status[11]- not used
183758 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
183798 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
183830  status[14]- Timeout occured
183859  status[15]- GPIB error detected
183893 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
184146 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
184456 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
184569   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
184617  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
184664  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device. 
184788 GPIB status vector:
184809 status[0] - Device Clear State
184840  status[1] - Device Trigger State
184874  status[2] - Listener Active State
184910 status[3] - Talker Active State
184943 status[4] - Attention line asserted
184980 status[5] -
184992 Controller In Charge
185013  status[6] - Remote State
185039  status[7] - Lockout State
185067 status[8] - I/O Completed 
185095 status[9] - not used
185116  status[10]- not used
185138  status[11]- not used
185161 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
185201 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
185233  status[14]- Timeout occured
185262  status[15]- GPIB error detected

258603 InitVXIlibrary.vi
258628 Initializes the NI-VXI library and reads in the resource manager table. The library is automatically initialized when any VXI VI is used in a diagram. If you initialize the library with this VI, you must call CloseVXIlibrary later in your diagram.

291095      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

331127 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
331466 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
331724      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
331775      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
331822      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
331880      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
331937      error, and a positive value is a warning.
331985      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
332032      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
332081 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI."

The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
332551      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

390129      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

390342      error, and a positive value is a warning.

433947 MakeAddr.vi

437146 MUUUU
437433 RSRC
437440 LVINLBVWgH
437458 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
437766 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
438042 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
438387 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

482749 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information. 593710 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

633947 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
634199 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
634544      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
634596      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
634654      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
634711      error, and a positive value is a warning.
634759      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
634809      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
634858 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

743651 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
743996      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
744048      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
744106      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
744163      error, and a positive value is a warning.
744211      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
744261      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
744310 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
744450 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
744680 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
744727 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
744758 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
744816 Optional Parameter Default Values:
744851     bd - GPIB board (0)
744875     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
744916     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
744961     logical addr - VXI logical address 
745002 EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
745100 INSTR{GPIB::5}"

745148 (ABC) 
745155 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
745338 (I32) 
745345 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
745596 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
745854      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
745905      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
745952      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
746010      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
746067      error, and a positive value is a warning.
746115      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
746162      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
746211 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

874405 device
874419 port number
874434 port width (8)@
874452 pattern
874463 iteration (0:initialize)
874503 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
874682 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
874810 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
875033 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
875168 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
875416 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
875599 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
875992 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
876145 J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
876479 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

902050 Oldest compatible LabVIEW.
902116 device
902130 port number@
902145 pattern
902156 port width (8)
902174 iteration (0:initialize)
902214 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
902393 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
902484 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
902718 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
902854 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
903103 &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
903263 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
903656 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
903810 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
904147 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1007527  INSTRUCTIONS:
1007543 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1008303 Other Uses:
1008317 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1008697 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1008954 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
1009528 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

1011617 message
1011632 GetCommErr"
1011664 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
1012229 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
1012400 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
1012515 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
1012650 displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
1012803 HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
1012873 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
1012971 error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
1013130 user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
1013350 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
1013568 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
1013616 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
1013741 error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
1013886 exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
1014082 (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
1014145 cancels error under the following conditions:
1014193 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
1014533 sets error under the following conditions:
1014578 If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
1014891 jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
1014997 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1015171 51code is the error code associated with an error.
1015224 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1015377 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
1015501 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1015675 51code is the error code associated with an error.
1015728 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1015881 mimessage describes the error code that occurred, the source of the error, and a description of the error.

If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1020465 Other Uses:
1020479 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1020859 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1021116 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  H

1072488 For most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
1072593 This VI establishes a port configuration. You can use the task ID that this VI returns only in digital port VIs.
1072707 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
1072976 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
1073141 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
1073539 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
1074117 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
1074260 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
1074460      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1074512      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1074570      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1074628      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1074676      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1074726      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1074775 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
1074896 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module.
1075223 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1075463 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
1075808      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1075860      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1075918      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1075976      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1076024      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1076074      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1076123 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1076172 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

1104542 This VI reads the port identified by task ID and returns the pattern read.
1104618 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
1104787 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.
1105361 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
1105561      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1105613      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1105671      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1105729      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1105777      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1105827      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1105876 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
1105996 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

1369749 Mode
1369767 This vi performs general purpose RS-232 communication.
1369822 Timeout: (value in seconds)
1369850 Mode:
1369856 0 = write then read, 1 = write only, 2 = read only
1369907 Port Select:
1369920 0 = com1, 1 = com2
1369941 |error in is a cluster that describes the error status before this VI executes. If error in indicates that an error occurred before this VI was called, this VI may choose not to execute its function, but just pass the error through to its error out cluster. If no error has occurred, then this VI executes normally and sets its own error status in error out. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
1370580 status is TRUE if an error occurred before this VI was called, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code.
1370769 code is the number identifying an error or warning. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code. Use the error handler VIs to look up the meaning of this code and to display the corresponding error message.
1371038 source is a string that indicates the origin of the error, if any. Usually source is the name of the VI in which the error occurred.
1371173 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. Otherwise, error out shows the error, if any, that occurred in this VI. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
1371687 status is TRUE if an error occurred, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code.

1439367 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. Otherwise, error out shows the error, if any, that occurred in this VI. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
1439881 status is TRUE if an error occurred, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code.
1440044 code is the number identifying an error or warning. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code. Use the error handler VIs to look up the meaning of this code and to display the corresponding error message.
1440313 source is a string that indicates the origin of the error, if any. Usually source is the name of the VI in which the error occurred."

1457921 When you use the serial port VIs on a Sun SPARCstation, the port number parameter is 0 for /dev/ttya, 1 for /dev/ttyb, and so on.
1458051 On the Macintosh, port 0 is the modem, using the drivers .ain and .aout. Port 1 is the printer, using the drivers.bin and .bout. To get more ports on a Macintosh, you must install other boards, with the accompanying drivers.
1458276 UQbyte count is the number of bytes currently queued up in the serial port buffer.
1458362 .error code. If error code is non-zero, an error occurred. Refer to Appendix C, Error Codes, for a list of error codes.

1475153 When you use the serial port VIs on a Sun SPARCstation, the port number parameter is 0 for /dev/ttya, 1 for /dev/ttyb, and so on.

1475511 Wrequested byte count specifies the number of characters to be read. If you want to read all of the characters currently at the serial port, first execute the Bytes at Serial Port VI to determine the exact number of bytes ready to be read. Then use the byte count output of that VI as the requested byte count input to the Serial Port Read VI.

1556480 Computes the mean value and the standard deviation (STD) of the values in the input sequence X. The mean and standard deviation are computed using the following formulas:
1556652       mean = Sum { X[i] } / n.
1556684       STD = sqrt( Sum{ (X[i] - mean)^2 } / n ).NJX. If the input sequence X is empty, standard deviation and mean are NaN.

1593824 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
1594120 Computes the mean value and the standard deviation (STD) of the values in the input sequence X. The mean and standard deviation are computed using the following formulas:
1594292       mean = Sum { X[i] } / n.
1594324       STD = sqrt( Sum{ (X[i] - mean)^2 } / n ).
1594379 QWrites the data in string to write to the serial port indicated in port number. 
1594471 qReads the number of characters specified by requested byte count from the serial port indicated in port number. 
1594595 kReturns in byte count the number of bytes in the input buffer of the serial port indicated in port number.

1596187 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
1596760 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1596939 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
1597030 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
1597264 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
1597400 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.
1597536 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1597715 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
1597843 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
1598066 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.

1610385 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
1610673 (I32) 
1610680 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
1610931 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
1611189      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1611240      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
1611287      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1611345      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
1611402      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1611450      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
1611497      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1611548 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
1611649 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1611753 The code input identifies the error or warning.
1611802 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1611906 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
1611971 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1612077 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
1612422      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1612474      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1612532      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
1612589      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1612637      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1612687      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1612738 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
1612839 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1612943 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
1613008 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1613112 The code input identifies the error or warning.
1613161 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

1645915 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
1646260      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1646312      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1646370      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
1646427      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1646475      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1646525      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1646576 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
1646677 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1646781 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
1646846 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1646950 The code input identifies the error or warning.
1646999 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

1647362      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

1726068 1) Plug in and turn on LC103 Mainboard test box.

1726167     Mainboard tester (#74C216-1).
